the Lounge for Two Brothers Trivia Night!

LUKE ELDER ’13
Position: Conservation Intern for !e Nature 
Conservancy on Martha’s Vineyard, Mass.
Job description:  Land stewardship and man-
agement, invasive species control, native plant 
nursery work, vegetation monitoring, involve-
ment with ongoing studies by the TNC Island Of-
"ce, wildlife biology work, bird surveys, a study 
on river otters and some bat monitoring.
THOUGHTS: “I learned a great deal about what 
it means to have a "eld job. My previous envi-
ronmental or conservation work experience has 
only been composed of o#ce research jobs, but 
working for TNC in the "eld truly showed me 
what it takes day-to-day to be a "eld biologist. 
For anyone interested in biology, botany, ecol-
ogy, land conservation and management, I would 
highly recommend this internship. !e experi-
ence taught me a lot about botany and plant 
work, something that I had never really been 
exposed to before. Getting the experience to help 
me navigate through "guring out what I like and 
what I don’t like was extremely helpful in terms 
of moving forward with "nding a job a$er gradu-
ation.”
TipS: “I would suggest talking to faculty or sta% 
who are active in the "eld you are interested in, 
and networking with them and their connections. 
!e EIA is also a great resource when it comes to 
polishing your resume, writing a cover letter or 
practicing for an interview.”
Top cover letter TipS: “[Include:] 1) why you 
are interested or passionate about the position, 
2) what background and education you have that 
quali"es you speci"cally for the position and 3) 
not only what you’ll bring to the position, but 
what you’ll take away from it.”
Interview reminders: “I "nd it helpful to 
really research both the company and position 
you are applying for, and to really be comfortable 
talking about both. Also, always be polite, friend-
ly and yourself.”

AVOID THESE MISTAKES  
Rana abdelhamid ’15
 Position #1: “With funding from EIA, I volun-
teered at Centro Para Los Adolescentes De San 
Miguel De Allende.”
Job description: “I had the chance to teach self 
defense, with another student at Middlebury, to 
youth leaders who would in turn teach the tech-
niques to women. !rough these classes, I was able 
to form friendships with many of the youth lead-
ers and learn about their experiences in Mexico. I 
was also able to connect with and establish many 
relationships with the women I met in the local 
villages.”
Position #2: Intern for the national o#ce for Am-
nesty International USA
Job description#2: “I worked on various human 
rights campaigns and helped conduct research on 
massive uprisings and social movements around 
the globe by connecting with the leaders of these 
movements.”
TipS: “Don’t be afraid to propose a project and 
take initiative. If there is an organization that you 
may be interested in working with, then reach out 
to them with ways in which you can contribute to 
their programming. !is way the relationship is 
two-way — you are o%ering something and learn-
ing at the same time.”
Interview reminders: “During an interview I 
feel like it is really important to be candid and be 
yourself. If your personality doesn’t "t the culture 
of the organization then you probably would not be 
comfortable there anyway!”
OWEN WITEK ’13
Position: Legislative Intern for Senator Patty Mur-
ray in her Washington, D.C. o#ce
Job description: “My daily tasks ranged from the 
mundane — answering phones, re"lling printers, 
running errands, giving Capitol tours — to the very 
interesting — attending hearings, doing research on 
legislation, writing memos, compiling brie"ng books.
THOUGHTS: “Going into the summer my main goal 
was to simply experience working in politics for an 
elected o#cial.  It was basically a trial run to see if 
this was really what I wanted to spend the rest of my 
career doing. Honestly it was everything I hoped it 
would be and more. I met some of really interesting 
and fun people, learned a ton and most importantly 
had a blast coming to work every day in such hal-
lowed halls.”
TipS: “It is important to apply lots of di%erent places 
and really put your e%ort into every single applica-
tion.”
Top cover letter TipS: “Little things like spell-
ing mistakes in your cover letter or awkward resume 
formatting can be the di%erence between getting 
into your ideal internship and not. !e people who 
read these are very busy and they have a large pool to 
choose from.”
Interview reminders: “I think its good to show 
that you are applying with a real purpose and plan in 
mind for the future. Far too many people only ap-
ply to internships so they will have something to do 
over the summer and interviewers can see that right 
away. !at being said, it’s okay to not know all of the 
answers. !ey are looking for people who are fast 
learners and can pick up the &ow of the workplace, 
not people who think they know everything about 
everything already.”
Jenny johnston ’14
Position: Intern for the Corporate Development Group at BlackRock, the 
largest investment management company in the world
Job description: “I not only witnessed the entire process of an acquisition, 
but I was an integral part of the valuations, conversations and strategy of the 
execution. With a little intrinsic motivation, a curious mind and a support-
ive team, I was able to contribute and take ownership in ways I did not think 
were going to happen at the beginning of the summer.”
THOUGHTS: “First and foremost, you are only going to get out of [the intern-
ship] what you put in. !ere were de"nitely days when I wanted to go home 
and sleep but I found that it was in the hours when I was in the o#ce with 
the analyst on the team that I learned the most. Second, attention to detail. It 
is a world of perfectionists. !ird, stay positive. !is past summer tested my 
ability to turn harsh criticism into positive motivation to better myself. !ere 
were certainly days that were very hard and the days of "ve hours or less of 
sleep caused me to search for any quick "x of sugar (Snickers and dark choco-
late M&Ms were my downfall) to fake a sense of energy but if you stay posi-
tive you will make it through and with a greater sense of accomplishment.”
At times I felt burnt out, a$er trying very hard to get an internship for my 
sophomore summer I wasn’t sure I was going to want to do it again, but with 
each resume and cover letter sent you learn what is important, how to present 
yourself and how to be more successful the next time.”
TipS: “!e more and more I have spoken with people about their jobs, and 
read about [the endeavours of] Midd alums, the more I have been able to 
narrow down what and where it is I think I will be able to best contribute and 
as well enjoy myself.”
Top cover letter TipS: “Be precise, demonstrate your knowledge, be per-
suasive.”
Interview reminders: “At "rst I had a really hard time if I couldn’t make 
my interviewer laugh. If they hadn’t cracked a smile I would get nervous, feel 
as though something was wrong and start to ramble — bad. Not everyone 
has the same sense of humor and so I had to adjust. Landing an internship is 
about connecting with the people at the company and if for some reason you 
don’t connect most likely you wouldn’t enjoy your time there anyways: you 
spend the majority of your time with them [so] it’s more about the people.
